| `npm run prisma:studio` | Open Prisma Studio to view data |

## 📝 Environment Variables

### Setup Variables (Optional - for custom admin credentials)

Set these **before** running `npm run db:setup` if your PostgreSQL uses different admin credentials:

```bash
# Windows PowerShell
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_admin_user"
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_admin_password"

# Windows CMD
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=your_admin_user
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=your_admin_password
```

**Defaults:**
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres`
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres`
- `DB_HOST=localhost`
- `DB_PORT=5432`

### Generated Variables (Auto-written to .env)

After running `npm run db:setup`, your `.env` file will contain:

```env
# Database Configuration (Auto-generated by setup-postgres.js)
POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres
POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres
DB_HOST=localhost
DB_PORT=5432
DB_NAME=emdad_3pl
DB_USER=emdad_3pl_app
DB_PASSWORD=<32-character-hex-password>
DATABASE_URL="postgresql://emdad_3pl_app:<password>@localhost:5432/emdad_3pl?schema=public"
```

## 🔌 How Backend Reads Database Configuration

**Connection Flow:**
```
.env or .env.local
  ↓
DATABASE_URL environment variable
  ↓
Prisma schema.prisma (datasource db { url = env("DATABASE_URL") })
  ↓
PrismaClient (generated)
  ↓
PrismaService (extends PrismaClient)
  ↓
Application Code (inventory.service.ts, etc.)
```

**Key Points:**
- NestJS `ConfigModule` loads `.env.local` (preferred) or `.env` (fallback)
- Prisma reads `DATABASE_URL` from environment
- All database operations go through `PrismaService`

## ✅ Setup Steps

1. **Ensure PostgreSQL is running** on your local machine

2. **Set admin credentials** (if different from defaults):
   ```powershell
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_user"
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_password"
   ```

3. **Run setup**:
   ```bash
   npm run db:setup
   ```

4. **Generate Prisma client**:
   ```bash
   npm run prisma:generate
   ```

5. **Seed database** (optional):
   ```bash
   npm run db:seed
   ```

6. **Start server**:
   ```bash
   npm run start:dev
   ```

## 🔍 Verification

After setup, verify everything works:

```bash
# Test connection
npm run db:check

# View data in Prisma Studio
npm run prisma:studio

# Test API endpoint
# Start server, then: GET http://localhost:3000/inventory/current-stock
```

## 🛠️ Troubleshooting

### "password authentication failed"
- Your PostgreSQL admin credentials are incorrect
- Set `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER` and `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD` before running setup

### "connection refused"
- PostgreSQL is not running
- Check if PostgreSQL service is started
- Verify it's listening on port 5432

### "database already exists"
- Normal if you've run setup before
- Script will skip creation and continue
- Use `npm run db:reset` to start fresh

## 📚 Additional Documentation

- **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup instructions and troubleshooting
- **`QUICK_START.md`** - General project quick start
- **`DATABASE_SETUP.md`** - Manual setup alternatives

## 🎉 You're Ready!

The database setup is fully automated. Just run `npm run db:setup` and you're done!

- **Database Password**: Randomly generated secure password (32 hex characters)
- **Host**: `localhost`
- **Port**: `5432`

## 🚀 Quick Start Command

```bash
cd server
npm run db:setup
```

**That's it!** The script handles everything automatically.

## 📁 Files Created

### Setup Scripts
1. **`scripts/setup-postgres.js`** - Main automated setup script
   - Creates database user
   - Creates database
   - Grants privileges
   - Runs schema.sql
   - Updates .env file

2. **`scripts/reset-database.js`** - Database reset script
   - Drops and recreates database
   - Useful for development resets

3. **`scripts/check-postgres.js`** - Connection test script
   - Verifies PostgreSQL connectivity

### Configuration Files
4. **`.env.example`** - Environment variables template
   - Shows all required variables
   - Safe to commit to version control

### Documentation
5. **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup guide
6. **`DATABASE_SETUP_SUMMARY.md`** - Quick reference
7. **`POSTGRES_SETUP_COMPLETE.md`** - This file

### Updated Files
8. **`package.json`** - Added database scripts:
   - `db:setup` - Full setup
   - `db:reset` - Reset database
   - `db:check` - Test connection
   - `db:seed` - Seed fake data

## 🔧 Available NPM Scripts

| Command | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `npm run db:setup` | **Full automated setup** - Creates user, database, runs schema |
| `npm run db:reset` | Drop and recreate database (WARNING: deletes all data) |
| `npm run db:check` | Test PostgreSQL connection |
| `npm run db:seed` | Seed database with fake data |
| `npm run prisma:generate` | Generate Prisma client after setup |
| `npm run prisma:studio` | Open Prisma Studio to view data |

## 📝 Environment Variables

### Setup Variables (Optional - for custom admin credentials)

Set these **before** running `npm run db:setup` if your PostgreSQL uses different admin credentials:

```bash
# Windows PowerShell
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_admin_user"
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_admin_password"

# Windows CMD
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=your_admin_user
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=your_admin_password
```

**Defaults:**
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres`
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres`
- `DB_HOST=localhost`
- `DB_PORT=5432`

### Generated Variables (Auto-written to .env)

After running `npm run db:setup`, your `.env` file will contain:

```env
# Database Configuration (Auto-generated by setup-postgres.js)
POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres
POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres
DB_HOST=localhost
DB_PORT=5432
DB_NAME=emdad_3pl
DB_USER=emdad_3pl_app
DB_PASSWORD=<32-character-hex-password>
DATABASE_URL="postgresql://emdad_3pl_app:<password>@localhost:5432/emdad_3pl?schema=public"
```

## 🔌 How Backend Reads Database Configuration

**Connection Flow:**
```
.env or .env.local
  ↓
DATABASE_URL environment variable
  ↓
Prisma schema.prisma (datasource db { url = env("DATABASE_URL") })
  ↓
PrismaClient (generated)
  ↓
PrismaService (extends PrismaClient)
  ↓
Application Code (inventory.service.ts, etc.)
```

**Key Points:**
- NestJS `ConfigModule` loads `.env.local` (preferred) or `.env` (fallback)
- Prisma reads `DATABASE_URL` from environment
- All database operations go through `PrismaService`

## ✅ Setup Steps

1. **Ensure PostgreSQL is running** on your local machine

2. **Set admin credentials** (if different from defaults):
   ```powershell
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_user"
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_password"
   ```

3. **Run setup**:
   ```bash
   npm run db:setup
   ```

4. **Generate Prisma client**:
   ```bash
   npm run prisma:generate
   ```

5. **Seed database** (optional):
   ```bash
   npm run db:seed
   ```

6. **Start server**:
   ```bash
   npm run start:dev
   ```

## 🔍 Verification

After setup, verify everything works:

```bash
# Test connection
npm run db:check

# View data in Prisma Studio
npm run prisma:studio

# Test API endpoint
# Start server, then: GET http://localhost:3000/inventory/current-stock
```

## 🛠️ Troubleshooting

### "password authentication failed"
- Your PostgreSQL admin credentials are incorrect
- Set `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER` and `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD` before running setup

### "connection refused"
- PostgreSQL is not running
- Check if PostgreSQL service is started
- Verify it's listening on port 5432

### "database already exists"
- Normal if you've run setup before
- Script will skip creation and continue
- Use `npm run db:reset` to start fresh

## 📚 Additional Documentation

- **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup instructions and troubleshooting
- **`QUICK_START.md`** - General project quick start
- **`DATABASE_SETUP.md`** - Manual setup alternatives

## 🎉 You're Ready!

The database setup is fully automated. Just run `npm run db:setup` and you're done!

   npm run db:setup
   ```

4. **Generate Prisma client**:
   ```bash
   npm run prisma:generate
   ```

5. **Seed database** (optional):
   ```bash
   npm run db:seed
   ```

6. **Start server**:
   ```bash
   npm run start:dev
   ```

## 🔍 Verification

After setup, verify everything works:

```bash
# Test connection
npm run db:check

# View data in Prisma Studio
npm run prisma:studio

# Test API endpoint
# Start server, then: GET http://localhost:3000/inventory/current-stock
```

## 🛠️ Troubleshooting

### "password authentication failed"
- Your PostgreSQL admin credentials are incorrect
- Set `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER` and `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD` before running setup

### "connection refused"
- PostgreSQL is not running
- Check if PostgreSQL service is started
- Verify it's listening on port 5432

### "database already exists"
- Normal if you've run setup before
- Script will skip creation and continue
- Use `npm run db:reset` to start fresh

## 📚 Additional Documentation

- **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup instructions and troubleshooting
- **`QUICK_START.md`** - General project quick start
- **`DATABASE_SETUP.md`** - Manual setup alternatives

## 🎉 You're Ready!

The database setup is fully automated. Just run `npm run db:setup` and you're done!










## 🎯 Summary

Automated PostgreSQL database setup has been configured for the Emdad 3PL WMS backend. All scripts and configuration files are ready to use.

## 📋 Generated Database Credentials

When you run the setup script, it will automatically generate:

- **Database Name**: `emdad_3pl`
- **Database User**: `emdad_3pl_app`  
- **Database Password**: Randomly generated secure password (32 hex characters)
- **Host**: `localhost`
- **Port**: `5432`

## 🚀 Quick Start Command

```bash
cd server
npm run db:setup
```

**That's it!** The script handles everything automatically.

## 📁 Files Created

### Setup Scripts
1. **`scripts/setup-postgres.js`** - Main automated setup script
   - Creates database user
   - Creates database
   - Grants privileges
   - Runs schema.sql
   - Updates .env file

2. **`scripts/reset-database.js`** - Database reset script
   - Drops and recreates database
   - Useful for development resets

3. **`scripts/check-postgres.js`** - Connection test script
   - Verifies PostgreSQL connectivity

### Configuration Files
4. **`.env.example`** - Environment variables template
   - Shows all required variables
   - Safe to commit to version control

### Documentation
5. **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup guide
6. **`DATABASE_SETUP_SUMMARY.md`** - Quick reference
7. **`POSTGRES_SETUP_COMPLETE.md`** - This file

### Updated Files
8. **`package.json`** - Added database scripts:
   - `db:setup` - Full setup
   - `db:reset` - Reset database
   - `db:check` - Test connection
   - `db:seed` - Seed fake data

## 🔧 Available NPM Scripts

| Command | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `npm run db:setup` | **Full automated setup** - Creates user, database, runs schema |
| `npm run db:reset` | Drop and recreate database (WARNING: deletes all data) |
| `npm run db:check` | Test PostgreSQL connection |
| `npm run db:seed` | Seed database with fake data |
| `npm run prisma:generate` | Generate Prisma client after setup |
| `npm run prisma:studio` | Open Prisma Studio to view data |

## 📝 Environment Variables

### Setup Variables (Optional - for custom admin credentials)

Set these **before** running `npm run db:setup` if your PostgreSQL uses different admin credentials:

```bash
# Windows PowerShell
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_admin_user"
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_admin_password"

# Windows CMD
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=your_admin_user
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=your_admin_password
```

**Defaults:**
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres`
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres`
- `DB_HOST=localhost`
- `DB_PORT=5432`

### Generated Variables (Auto-written to .env)

After running `npm run db:setup`, your `.env` file will contain:

```env
# Database Configuration (Auto-generated by setup-postgres.js)
POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres
POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres
DB_HOST=localhost
DB_PORT=5432
DB_NAME=emdad_3pl
DB_USER=emdad_3pl_app
DB_PASSWORD=<32-character-hex-password>
DATABASE_URL="postgresql://emdad_3pl_app:<password>@localhost:5432/emdad_3pl?schema=public"
```

## 🔌 How Backend Reads Database Configuration

**Connection Flow:**
```
.env or .env.local
  ↓
DATABASE_URL environment variable
  ↓
Prisma schema.prisma (datasource db { url = env("DATABASE_URL") })
  ↓
PrismaClient (generated)
  ↓
PrismaService (extends PrismaClient)
  ↓
Application Code (inventory.service.ts, etc.)
```

**Key Points:**
- NestJS `ConfigModule` loads `.env.local` (preferred) or `.env` (fallback)
- Prisma reads `DATABASE_URL` from environment
- All database operations go through `PrismaService`

## ✅ Setup Steps

1. **Ensure PostgreSQL is running** on your local machine

2. **Set admin credentials** (if different from defaults):
   ```powershell
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_user"
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_password"
   ```

3. **Run setup**:
   ```bash
   npm run db:setup
   ```

4. **Generate Prisma client**:
   ```bash
   npm run prisma:generate
   ```

5. **Seed database** (optional):
   ```bash
   npm run db:seed
   ```

6. **Start server**:
   ```bash
   npm run start:dev
   ```

## 🔍 Verification

After setup, verify everything works:

```bash
# Test connection
npm run db:check

# View data in Prisma Studio
npm run prisma:studio

# Test API endpoint
# Start server, then: GET http://localhost:3000/inventory/current-stock
```

- Verify it's listening on port 5432

- Script will skip creation and continue

- `DB_HOST=localhost`
- `DB_PORT=5432`

### Generated Variables (Auto-written to .env)

After running `npm run db:setup`, your `.env` file will contain:

```env
# Database Configuration (Auto-generated by setup-postgres.js)
POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres
POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres
DB_HOST=localhost
DB_PORT=5432
DB_NAME=emdad_3pl
DB_USER=emdad_3pl_app
DB_PASSWORD=<32-character-hex-password>
DATABASE_URL="postgresql://emdad_3pl_app:<password>@localhost:5432/emdad_3pl?schema=public"
```

## 🔌 How Backend Reads Database Configuration

**Connection Flow:**
```
.env or .env.local
  ↓
DATABASE_URL environment variable
  ↓
Prisma schema.prisma (datasource db { url = env("DATABASE_URL") })
  ↓
PrismaClient (generated)
  ↓
PrismaService (extends PrismaClient)
  ↓
Application Code (inventory.service.ts, etc.)
```

**Key Points:**
- NestJS `ConfigModule` loads `.env.local` (preferred) or `.env` (fallback)
- Prisma reads `DATABASE_URL` from environment
- All database operations go through `PrismaService`

## ✅ Setup Steps

1. **Ensure PostgreSQL is running** on your local machine

2. **Set admin credentials** (if different from defaults):
   ```powershell
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_user"
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_password"
   ```

3. **Run setup**:
   ```bash
   npm run db:setup
   ```

4. **Generate Prisma client**:
   ```bash
   npm run prisma:generate
   ```

5. **Seed database** (optional):
   ```bash
   npm run db:seed
   ```

6. **Start server**:
   ```bash
   npm run start:dev
   ```

## 🔍 Verification

After setup, verify everything works:

```bash
# Test connection
npm run db:check

# View data in Prisma Studio
npm run prisma:studio

# Test API endpoint
# Start server, then: GET http://localhost:3000/inventory/current-stock
```

## 🛠️ Troubleshooting

### "password authentication failed"
- Your PostgreSQL admin credentials are incorrect
- Set `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER` and `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD` before running setup

### "connection refused"
- PostgreSQL is not running
- Check if PostgreSQL service is started
- Verify it's listening on port 5432

### "database already exists"
- Normal if you've run setup before
- Script will skip creation and continue
- Use `npm run db:reset` to start fresh

## 📚 Additional Documentation

- **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup instructions and troubleshooting
- **`QUICK_START.md`** - General project quick start
- **`DATABASE_SETUP.md`** - Manual setup alternatives

## 🎉 You're Ready!

The database setup is fully automated. Just run `npm run db:setup` and you're done!

















## 🎯 Summary

Automated PostgreSQL database setup has been configured for the Emdad 3PL WMS backend. All scripts and configuration files are ready to use.

## 📋 Generated Database Credentials

When you run the setup script, it will automatically generate:

- **Database Name**: `emdad_3pl`
- **Database User**: `emdad_3pl_app`  
- **Database Password**: Randomly generated secure password (32 hex characters)
- **Host**: `localhost`
- **Port**: `5432`

## 🚀 Quick Start Command

```bash
cd server
npm run db:setup
```

## 📁 Files Created

### Setup Scripts
1. **`scripts/setup-postgres.js`** - Main automated setup script
   - Creates database user
   - Creates database
   - Grants privileges
   - Runs schema.sql
   - Updates .env file

2. **`scripts/reset-database.js`** - Database reset script
   - Drops and recreates database
   - Useful for development resets

3. **`scripts/check-postgres.js`** - Connection test script
   - Verifies PostgreSQL connectivity

### Configuration Files
4. **`.env.example`** - Environment variables template
   - Shows all required variables
   - Safe to commit to version control

7. **`POSTGRES_SETUP_COMPLETE.md`** - This file

   - `db:setup` - Full setup
   - `db:reset` - Reset database
   - `db:check` - Test connection
   - `db:seed` - Seed fake data

## 🔧 Available NPM Scripts

| Command | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `npm run db:setup` | **Full automated setup** - Creates user, database, runs schema |
| `npm run db:reset` | Drop and recreate database (WARNING: deletes all data) |
| `npm run db:check` | Test PostgreSQL connection |
| `npm run db:seed` | Seed database with fake data |
| `npm run prisma:generate` | Generate Prisma client after setup |
| `npm run prisma:studio` | Open Prisma Studio to view data |

$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_admin_password"

# Windows CMD

set POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=your_admin_password
```

- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres`
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres`
- `DB_HOST=localhost`
- `DB_PORT=5432`

   - Verifies PostgreSQL connectivity

### Configuration Files
4. **`.env.example`** - Environment variables template
   - Shows all required variables
   - Safe to commit to version control

### Documentation
5. **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup guide
6. **`DATABASE_SETUP_SUMMARY.md`** - Quick reference
7. **`POSTGRES_SETUP_COMPLETE.md`** - This file

### Updated Files
8. **`package.json`** - Added database scripts:
   - `db:setup` - Full setup
   - `db:reset` - Reset database
   - `db:check` - Test connection
   - `db:seed` - Seed fake data

## 🔧 Available NPM Scripts

| Command | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `npm run db:setup` | **Full automated setup** - Creates user, database, runs schema |
| `npm run db:reset` | Drop and recreate database (WARNING: deletes all data) |
| `npm run db:check` | Test PostgreSQL connection |
| `npm run db:seed` | Seed database with fake data |
| `npm run prisma:generate` | Generate Prisma client after setup |
| `npm run prisma:studio` | Open Prisma Studio to view data |

## 📝 Environment Variables

### Setup Variables (Optional - for custom admin credentials)

Set these **before** running `npm run db:setup` if your PostgreSQL uses different admin credentials:

```bash
# Windows PowerShell
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_admin_user"
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_admin_password"

# Windows CMD
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=your_admin_user
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=your_admin_password
```

**Defaults:**
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres`
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres`
- `DB_HOST=localhost`
- `DB_PORT=5432`

### Generated Variables (Auto-written to .env)

After running `npm run db:setup`, your `.env` file will contain:

```env
# Database Configuration (Auto-generated by setup-postgres.js)
POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres
POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres
DB_HOST=localhost
DB_PORT=5432
DB_NAME=emdad_3pl
DB_USER=emdad_3pl_app
DB_PASSWORD=<32-character-hex-password>
DATABASE_URL="postgresql://emdad_3pl_app:<password>@localhost:5432/emdad_3pl?schema=public"
```

## 🔌 How Backend Reads Database Configuration

**Connection Flow:**
```
.env or .env.local
  ↓
DATABASE_URL environment variable
  ↓
Prisma schema.prisma (datasource db { url = env("DATABASE_URL") })
  ↓
PrismaClient (generated)
  ↓
PrismaService (extends PrismaClient)
  ↓
Application Code (inventory.service.ts, etc.)
```

**Key Points:**
- NestJS `ConfigModule` loads `.env.local` (preferred) or `.env` (fallback)
- Prisma reads `DATABASE_URL` from environment
- All database operations go through `PrismaService`

## ✅ Setup Steps

1. **Ensure PostgreSQL is running** on your local machine

2. **Set admin credentials** (if different from defaults):
   ```powershell
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_user"
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_password"
   ```

3. **Run setup**:
   ```bash
   npm run db:setup
   ```

4. **Generate Prisma client**:
   ```bash
   npm run prisma:generate
   ```

5. **Seed database** (optional):
   ```bash
   npm run db:seed
   ```

6. **Start server**:
   ```bash
   npm run start:dev
   ```

## 🔍 Verification

After setup, verify everything works:

```bash
# Test connection
npm run db:check

# View data in Prisma Studio
npm run prisma:studio

# Test API endpoint
# Start server, then: GET http://localhost:3000/inventory/current-stock
```

## 🛠️ Troubleshooting

### "password authentication failed"
- Your PostgreSQL admin credentials are incorrect
- Set `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER` and `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD` before running setup

### "connection refused"
- PostgreSQL is not running
- Check if PostgreSQL service is started
- Verify it's listening on port 5432

### "database already exists"
- Normal if you've run setup before
- Script will skip creation and continue
- Use `npm run db:reset` to start fresh

## 📚 Additional Documentation

- **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup instructions and troubleshooting
- **`QUICK_START.md`** - General project quick start
- **`DATABASE_SETUP.md`** - Manual setup alternatives

## 🎉 You're Ready!

The database setup is fully automated. Just run `npm run db:setup` and you're done!

- Set `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER` and `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD` before running setup

### "connection refused"
- PostgreSQL is not running
- Check if PostgreSQL service is started
- Verify it's listening on port 5432

### "database already exists"
- Normal if you've run setup before
- Script will skip creation and continue
- Use `npm run db:reset` to start fresh

## 📚 Additional Documentation

- **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup instructions and troubleshooting
- **`QUICK_START.md`** - General project quick start
- **`DATABASE_SETUP.md`** - Manual setup alternatives

## 🎉 You're Ready!

The database setup is fully automated. Just run `npm run db:setup` and you're done!




## 🎯 Summary

Automated PostgreSQL database setup has been configured for the Emdad 3PL WMS backend. All scripts and configuration files are ready to use.

## 📋 Generated Database Credentials

When you run the setup script, it will automatically generate:

- **Database Name**: `emdad_3pl`
- **Database User**: `emdad_3pl_app`  
- **Database Password**: Randomly generated secure password (32 hex characters)
- **Host**: `localhost`
- **Port**: `5432`

## 🚀 Quick Start Command

```bash
cd server
npm run db:setup
```

**That's it!** The script handles everything automatically.

## 📁 Files Created

### Setup Scripts
1. **`scripts/setup-postgres.js`** - Main automated setup script
   - Creates database user
   - Creates database
   - Grants privileges
   - Runs schema.sql
   - Updates .env file

2. **`scripts/reset-database.js`** - Database reset script
   - Drops and recreates database
   - Useful for development resets

3. **`scripts/check-postgres.js`** - Connection test script
   - Verifies PostgreSQL connectivity

### Configuration Files
4. **`.env.example`** - Environment variables template
   - Shows all required variables
   - Safe to commit to version control

### Documentation
5. **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup guide
6. **`DATABASE_SETUP_SUMMARY.md`** - Quick reference
7. **`POSTGRES_SETUP_COMPLETE.md`** - This file

### Updated Files
8. **`package.json`** - Added database scripts:
   - `db:setup` - Full setup
   - `db:reset` - Reset database
   - `db:check` - Test connection
   - `db:seed` - Seed fake data

## 🔧 Available NPM Scripts

| Command | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `npm run db:setup` | **Full automated setup** - Creates user, database, runs schema |
| `npm run db:reset` | Drop and recreate database (WARNING: deletes all data) |
| `npm run db:check` | Test PostgreSQL connection |
| `npm run db:seed` | Seed database with fake data |
| `npm run prisma:generate` | Generate Prisma client after setup |
| `npm run prisma:studio` | Open Prisma Studio to view data |

## 📝 Environment Variables

### Setup Variables (Optional - for custom admin credentials)

Set these **before** running `npm run db:setup` if your PostgreSQL uses different admin credentials:

```bash
# Windows PowerShell
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_admin_user"
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_admin_password"

# Windows CMD
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=your_admin_user
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=your_admin_password
```

**Defaults:**
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres`
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres`
- `DB_HOST=localhost`
- `DB_PORT=5432`

### Generated Variables (Auto-written to .env)

After running `npm run db:setup`, your `.env` file will contain:

```env
# Database Configuration (Auto-generated by setup-postgres.js)
POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres
POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres
DB_HOST=localhost
DB_PORT=5432
DB_NAME=emdad_3pl
DB_USER=emdad_3pl_app
DB_PASSWORD=<32-character-hex-password>
DATABASE_URL="postgresql://emdad_3pl_app:<password>@localhost:5432/emdad_3pl?schema=public"
```

## 🔌 How Backend Reads Database Configuration

**Connection Flow:**
```
.env or .env.local
  ↓
DATABASE_URL environment variable
  ↓
Prisma schema.prisma (datasource db { url = env("DATABASE_URL") })
  ↓
PrismaClient (generated)
  ↓
PrismaService (extends PrismaClient)
  ↓
Application Code (inventory.service.ts, etc.)
```

**Key Points:**
- NestJS `ConfigModule` loads `.env.local` (preferred) or `.env` (fallback)
- Prisma reads `DATABASE_URL` from environment
- All database operations go through `PrismaService`

## ✅ Setup Steps

1. **Ensure PostgreSQL is running** on your local machine

2. **Set admin credentials** (if different from defaults):
   ```powershell
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_user"
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_password"
   ```

3. **Run setup**:
   ```bash
   npm run db:setup
   ```

4. **Generate Prisma client**:
   ```bash
   npm run prisma:generate
   ```

5. **Seed database** (optional):
   ```bash
   npm run db:seed
   ```

6. **Start server**:
   ```bash
   npm run start:dev
   ```

## 🔍 Verification

After setup, verify everything works:

```bash
# Test connection
npm run db:check

# View data in Prisma Studio
npm run prisma:studio

# Test API endpoint
# Start server, then: GET http://localhost:3000/inventory/current-stock
```

## 🛠️ Troubleshooting

### "password authentication failed"
- Your PostgreSQL admin credentials are incorrect
- Set `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER` and `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD` before running setup

### "connection refused"
- PostgreSQL is not running
- Check if PostgreSQL service is started
- Verify it's listening on port 5432

### "database already exists"
- Normal if you've run setup before
- Script will skip creation and continue
- Use `npm run db:reset` to start fresh

- **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup instructions and troubleshooting
- **`QUICK_START.md`** - General project quick start
- **`DATABASE_SETUP.md`** - Manual setup alternatives

## 🔌 How Backend Reads Database Configuration

**Connection Flow:**
```
.env or .env.local
  ↓
DATABASE_URL environment variable
  ↓
Prisma schema.prisma (datasource db { url = env("DATABASE_URL") })
  ↓
PrismaClient (generated)
  ↓
PrismaService (extends PrismaClient)
  ↓
Application Code (inventory.service.ts, etc.)
```

**Key Points:**
- NestJS `ConfigModule` loads `.env.local` (preferred) or `.env` (fallback)
- Prisma reads `DATABASE_URL` from environment
- All database operations go through `PrismaService`

## ✅ Setup Steps

1. **Ensure PostgreSQL is running** on your local machine

2. **Set admin credentials** (if different from defaults):
   ```powershell
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_user"
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_password"
   ```

3. **Run setup**:
   ```bash
   npm run db:setup
   ```

4. **Generate Prisma client**:
   ```bash
   npm run prisma:generate
   ```

5. **Seed database** (optional):
   ```bash
   npm run db:seed
   ```

6. **Start server**:
   ```bash
   npm run start:dev
   ```

## 🔍 Verification

After setup, verify everything works:

```bash
# Test connection
npm run db:check

# View data in Prisma Studio
npm run prisma:studio

# Test API endpoint
# Start server, then: GET http://localhost:3000/inventory/current-stock
```

## 🛠️ Troubleshooting

### "password authentication failed"
- Your PostgreSQL admin credentials are incorrect
- Set `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER` and `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD` before running setup

### "connection refused"
- PostgreSQL is not running
- Check if PostgreSQL service is started
- Verify it's listening on port 5432

### "database already exists"
- Normal if you've run setup before
- Script will skip creation and continue
- Use `npm run db:reset` to start fresh

## 📚 Additional Documentation

- **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup instructions and troubleshooting
- **`QUICK_START.md`** - General project quick start
- **`DATABASE_SETUP.md`** - Manual setup alternatives

## 🎉 You're Ready!

The database setup is fully automated. Just run `npm run db:setup` and you're done!




## 🎯 Summary

Automated PostgreSQL database setup has been configured for the Emdad 3PL WMS backend. All scripts and configuration files are ready to use.

## 📋 Generated Database Credentials

When you run the setup script, it will automatically generate:

- **Database Name**: `emdad_3pl`
- **Database User**: `emdad_3pl_app`  
- **Database Password**: Randomly generated secure password (32 hex characters)
- **Host**: `localhost`
- **Port**: `5432`

## 🚀 Quick Start Command

```bash
cd server
npm run db:setup
```

**That's it!** The script handles everything automatically.

## 📁 Files Created

### Setup Scripts
1. **`scripts/setup-postgres.js`** - Main automated setup script
   - Creates database user
   - Creates database
   - Grants privileges
   - Runs schema.sql
   - Updates .env file

2. **`scripts/reset-database.js`** - Database reset script
   - Drops and recreates database
   - Useful for development resets

3. **`scripts/check-postgres.js`** - Connection test script
   - Verifies PostgreSQL connectivity

### Configuration Files
4. **`.env.example`** - Environment variables template
   - Shows all required variables
   - Safe to commit to version control

### Documentation
5. **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup guide
6. **`DATABASE_SETUP_SUMMARY.md`** - Quick reference
7. **`POSTGRES_SETUP_COMPLETE.md`** - This file

### Updated Files
8. **`package.json`** - Added database scripts:
   - `db:setup` - Full setup
   - `db:reset` - Reset database
   - `db:check` - Test connection
   - `db:seed` - Seed fake data

## 🔧 Available NPM Scripts

| Command | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `npm run db:setup` | **Full automated setup** - Creates user, database, runs schema |
| `npm run db:reset` | Drop and recreate database (WARNING: deletes all data) |
| `npm run db:check` | Test PostgreSQL connection |
| `npm run db:seed` | Seed database with fake data |
| `npm run prisma:generate` | Generate Prisma client after setup |
| `npm run prisma:studio` | Open Prisma Studio to view data |

## 📝 Environment Variables

### Setup Variables (Optional - for custom admin credentials)

Set these **before** running `npm run db:setup` if your PostgreSQL uses different admin credentials:

```bash
# Windows PowerShell
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_admin_user"
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_admin_password"

# Windows CMD
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=your_admin_user
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=your_admin_password
```

**Defaults:**
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres`
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres`
- `DB_HOST=localhost`
- `DB_PORT=5432`

### Generated Variables (Auto-written to .env)

After running `npm run db:setup`, your `.env` file will contain:

```env
# Database Configuration (Auto-generated by setup-postgres.js)
POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres
POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres
DB_HOST=localhost
DB_PORT=5432
DB_NAME=emdad_3pl
DB_USER=emdad_3pl_app
DB_PASSWORD=<32-character-hex-password>
DATABASE_URL="postgresql://emdad_3pl_app:<password>@localhost:5432/emdad_3pl?schema=public"
```

## 🔧 Available NPM Scripts

| Command | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `npm run db:setup` | **Full automated setup** - Creates user, database, runs schema |
| `npm run db:reset` | Drop and recreate database (WARNING: deletes all data) |
| `npm run db:check` | Test PostgreSQL connection |
| `npm run db:seed` | Seed database with fake data |
| `npm run prisma:generate` | Generate Prisma client after setup |
| `npm run prisma:studio` | Open Prisma Studio to view data |

## 📝 Environment Variables

### Setup Variables (Optional - for custom admin credentials)

Set these **before** running `npm run db:setup` if your PostgreSQL uses different admin credentials:

```bash
# Windows PowerShell
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_admin_user"
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_admin_password"

# Windows CMD
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=your_admin_user
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=your_admin_password
```

**Defaults:**
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres`
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres`
- `DB_HOST=localhost`
- `DB_PORT=5432`

### Generated Variables (Auto-written to .env)

After running `npm run db:setup`, your `.env` file will contain:

```env
# Database Configuration (Auto-generated by setup-postgres.js)
POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres
POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres
DB_HOST=localhost
DB_PORT=5432
DB_NAME=emdad_3pl
DB_USER=emdad_3pl_app
DB_PASSWORD=<32-character-hex-password>
DATABASE_URL="postgresql://emdad_3pl_app:<password>@localhost:5432/emdad_3pl?schema=public"
```

## 🔌 How Backend Reads Database Configuration

**Connection Flow:**
```
.env or .env.local
  ↓
DATABASE_URL environment variable
  ↓
Prisma schema.prisma (datasource db { url = env("DATABASE_URL") })
  ↓
PrismaClient (generated)
  ↓
PrismaService (extends PrismaClient)
  ↓
Application Code (inventory.service.ts, etc.)
```

**Key Points:**
- NestJS `ConfigModule` loads `.env.local` (preferred) or `.env` (fallback)
- Prisma reads `DATABASE_URL` from environment
- All database operations go through `PrismaService`

## ✅ Setup Steps

1. **Ensure PostgreSQL is running** on your local machine

2. **Set admin credentials** (if different from defaults):
   ```powershell
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_user"
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_password"
   ```

3. **Run setup**:
   ```bash
   npm run db:setup
   ```

4. **Generate Prisma client**:
   ```bash
   npm run prisma:generate
   ```

5. **Seed database** (optional):
   ```bash
   npm run db:seed
   ```

6. **Start server**:
   ```bash
   npm run start:dev
   ```

## 🔍 Verification

After setup, verify everything works:

```bash
# Test connection
npm run db:check

# View data in Prisma Studio
npm run prisma:studio

# Test API endpoint
# Start server, then: GET http://localhost:3000/inventory/current-stock
```

## 🛠️ Troubleshooting

### "password authentication failed"
- Your PostgreSQL admin credentials are incorrect
- Set `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER` and `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD` before running setup

### "connection refused"
- PostgreSQL is not running
- Check if PostgreSQL service is started
- Verify it's listening on port 5432

### "database already exists"
- Normal if you've run setup before
- Script will skip creation and continue
- Use `npm run db:reset` to start fresh

## 📚 Additional Documentation

- **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup instructions and troubleshooting
- **`QUICK_START.md`** - General project quick start
- **`DATABASE_SETUP.md`** - Manual setup alternatives

## 🎉 You're Ready!

The database setup is fully automated. Just run `npm run db:setup` and you're done!

The database setup is fully automated. Just run `npm run db:setup` and you're done!




## 🎯 Summary

Automated PostgreSQL database setup has been configured for the Emdad 3PL WMS backend. All scripts and configuration files are ready to use.

## 📋 Generated Database Credentials

When you run the setup script, it will automatically generate:

- **Database Name**: `emdad_3pl`
- **Database User**: `emdad_3pl_app`  
- **Database Password**: Randomly generated secure password (32 hex characters)
- **Host**: `localhost`
- **Port**: `5432`

## 🚀 Quick Start Command

```bash
cd server
npm run db:setup
```

**That's it!** The script handles everything automatically.

## 📁 Files Created

### Setup Scripts
1. **`scripts/setup-postgres.js`** - Main automated setup script
   - Creates database user
   - Creates database
   - Grants privileges
   - Runs schema.sql
   - Updates .env file

2. **`scripts/reset-database.js`** - Database reset script
   - Drops and recreates database
   - Useful for development resets

3. **`scripts/check-postgres.js`** - Connection test script
   - Verifies PostgreSQL connectivity

### Configuration Files
4. **`.env.example`** - Environment variables template
   - Shows all required variables
   - Safe to commit to version control

### Documentation
5. **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup guide
6. **`DATABASE_SETUP_SUMMARY.md`** - Quick reference
7. **`POSTGRES_SETUP_COMPLETE.md`** - This file

### Updated Files
8. **`package.json`** - Added database scripts:
   - `db:setup` - Full setup
   - `db:reset` - Reset database
   - `db:check` - Test connection
   - `db:seed` - Seed fake data

## 🔧 Available NPM Scripts

| Command | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `npm run db:setup` | **Full automated setup** - Creates user, database, runs schema |
| `npm run db:reset` | Drop and recreate database (WARNING: deletes all data) |
| `npm run db:check` | Test PostgreSQL connection |
| `npm run db:seed` | Seed database with fake data |
| `npm run prisma:generate` | Generate Prisma client after setup |
| `npm run prisma:studio` | Open Prisma Studio to view data |

## 📝 Environment Variables

### Setup Variables (Optional - for custom admin credentials)

Set these **before** running `npm run db:setup` if your PostgreSQL uses different admin credentials:

```bash
# Windows PowerShell
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_admin_user"
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_admin_password"

# Windows CMD
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=your_admin_user
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=your_admin_password
```

**Defaults:**
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres`
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres`
- `DB_HOST=localhost`
- `DB_PORT=5432`

### Generated Variables (Auto-written to .env)

After running `npm run db:setup`, your `.env` file will contain:

```env
# Database Configuration (Auto-generated by setup-postgres.js)
POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres
POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres
DB_HOST=localhost
DB_PORT=5432
DB_NAME=emdad_3pl
DB_USER=emdad_3pl_app
DB_PASSWORD=<32-character-hex-password>
DATABASE_URL="postgresql://emdad_3pl_app:<password>@localhost:5432/emdad_3pl?schema=public"
```

## 🔌 How Backend Reads Database Configuration

**Connection Flow:**
```
.env or .env.local
  ↓
DATABASE_URL environment variable
  ↓
Prisma schema.prisma (datasource db { url = env("DATABASE_URL") })
  ↓
PrismaClient (generated)
  ↓
PrismaService (extends PrismaClient)
  ↓
Application Code (inventory.service.ts, etc.)
```

**Key Points:**
- NestJS `ConfigModule` loads `.env.local` (preferred) or `.env` (fallback)
- Prisma reads `DATABASE_URL` from environment
- All database operations go through `PrismaService`

## ✅ Setup Steps

1. **Ensure PostgreSQL is running** on your local machine

2. **Set admin credentials** (if different from defaults):
   ```powershell
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_user"
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_password"
   ```

3. **Run setup**:
   ```bash
   npm run db:setup
   ```

4. **Generate Prisma client**:
   ```bash
   npm run prisma:generate
   ```

5. **Seed database** (optional):
   ```bash
   npm run db:seed
   ```

6. **Start server**:
   ```bash
   npm run start:dev
   ```

## 🔍 Verification

After setup, verify everything works:

```bash
# Test connection
npm run db:check

# View data in Prisma Studio
npm run prisma:studio

# Test API endpoint
# Start server, then: GET http://localhost:3000/inventory/current-stock
```

## 🛠️ Troubleshooting

### "password authentication failed"
- Your PostgreSQL admin credentials are incorrect
- Set `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER` and `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD` before running setup

### "connection refused"
- PostgreSQL is not running
- Check if PostgreSQL service is started
- Verify it's listening on port 5432

### "database already exists"
- Normal if you've run setup before
- Script will skip creation and continue
- Use `npm run db:reset` to start fresh

## 📚 Additional Documentation

- **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup instructions and troubleshooting
- **`QUICK_START.md`** - General project quick start
- **`DATABASE_SETUP.md`** - Manual setup alternatives

## 🎉 You're Ready!

The database setup is fully automated. Just run `npm run db:setup` and you're done!

- All database operations go through `PrismaService`

## ✅ Setup Steps

1. **Ensure PostgreSQL is running** on your local machine

2. **Set admin credentials** (if different from defaults):
   ```powershell
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_user"
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_password"
   ```

3. **Run setup**:
   ```bash
   npm run db:setup
   ```

4. **Generate Prisma client**:
   ```bash
   npm run prisma:generate
   ```

5. **Seed database** (optional):
   ```bash
   npm run db:seed
   ```

6. **Start server**:
   ```bash
   npm run start:dev
   ```

## 🔍 Verification

After setup, verify everything works:

```bash
# Test connection
npm run db:check

# View data in Prisma Studio
npm run prisma:studio

# Test API endpoint
# Start server, then: GET http://localhost:3000/inventory/current-stock
```

## 🛠️ Troubleshooting

### "password authentication failed"
- Your PostgreSQL admin credentials are incorrect
- Set `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER` and `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD` before running setup

### "connection refused"
- PostgreSQL is not running
- Check if PostgreSQL service is started
- Verify it's listening on port 5432

### "database already exists"
- Normal if you've run setup before
- Script will skip creation and continue
- Use `npm run db:reset` to start fresh

## 📚 Additional Documentation

- **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup instructions and troubleshooting
- **`QUICK_START.md`** - General project quick start
- **`DATABASE_SETUP.md`** - Manual setup alternatives

## 🎉 You're Ready!

The database setup is fully automated. Just run `npm run db:setup` and you're done!




## 🎯 Summary

Automated PostgreSQL database setup has been configured for the Emdad 3PL WMS backend. All scripts and configuration files are ready to use.

## 📋 Generated Database Credentials

When you run the setup script, it will automatically generate:

- **Database Name**: `emdad_3pl`
- **Database User**: `emdad_3pl_app`  
- **Database Password**: Randomly generated secure password (32 hex characters)
- **Host**: `localhost`
- **Port**: `5432`

## 🚀 Quick Start Command

```bash
cd server
npm run db:setup
```

**That's it!** The script handles everything automatically.

## 📁 Files Created

### Setup Scripts
1. **`scripts/setup-postgres.js`** - Main automated setup script
   - Creates database user
   - Creates database
   - Grants privileges
   - Runs schema.sql
   - Updates .env file

2. **`scripts/reset-database.js`** - Database reset script
   - Drops and recreates database
   - Useful for development resets

3. **`scripts/check-postgres.js`** - Connection test script
   - Verifies PostgreSQL connectivity

### Configuration Files
4. **`.env.example`** - Environment variables template
   - Shows all required variables
   - Safe to commit to version control

### Documentation
5. **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup guide
6. **`DATABASE_SETUP_SUMMARY.md`** - Quick reference
7. **`POSTGRES_SETUP_COMPLETE.md`** - This file

### Updated Files
8. **`package.json`** - Added database scripts:
   - `db:setup` - Full setup
   - `db:reset` - Reset database
   - `db:check` - Test connection
   - `db:seed` - Seed fake data

## 🔧 Available NPM Scripts

| Command | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `npm run db:setup` | **Full automated setup** - Creates user, database, runs schema |
| `npm run db:reset` | Drop and recreate database (WARNING: deletes all data) |
| `npm run db:check` | Test PostgreSQL connection |
| `npm run db:seed` | Seed database with fake data |
| `npm run prisma:generate` | Generate Prisma client after setup |
| `npm run prisma:studio` | Open Prisma Studio to view data |

## 📝 Environment Variables

### Setup Variables (Optional - for custom admin credentials)

Set these **before** running `npm run db:setup` if your PostgreSQL uses different admin credentials:

```bash
# Windows PowerShell
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_admin_user"
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_admin_password"

# Windows CMD
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=your_admin_user
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=your_admin_password
```

**Defaults:**
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres`
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres`
- `DB_HOST=localhost`
- `DB_PORT=5432`

### Generated Variables (Auto-written to .env)

After running `npm run db:setup`, your `.env` file will contain:

```env
# Database Configuration (Auto-generated by setup-postgres.js)
POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres
POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres
DB_HOST=localhost
DB_PORT=5432
DB_NAME=emdad_3pl
DB_USER=emdad_3pl_app
DB_PASSWORD=<32-character-hex-password>
DATABASE_URL="postgresql://emdad_3pl_app:<password>@localhost:5432/emdad_3pl?schema=public"
```

## 🔌 How Backend Reads Database Configuration

**Connection Flow:**
```
.env or .env.local
  ↓
DATABASE_URL environment variable
  ↓
Prisma schema.prisma (datasource db { url = env("DATABASE_URL") })
  ↓
PrismaClient (generated)
  ↓
PrismaService (extends PrismaClient)
  ↓
Application Code (inventory.service.ts, etc.)
```

**Key Points:**
- NestJS `ConfigModule` loads `.env.local` (preferred) or `.env` (fallback)
- Prisma reads `DATABASE_URL` from environment
- All database operations go through `PrismaService`

   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_password"
   ```

3. **Run setup**:
   ```bash
   npm run db:setup
   ```

4. **Generate Prisma client**:
   ```bash
   npm run prisma:generate
   ```

5. **Seed database** (optional):
   ```bash
   npm run db:seed
   ```

6. **Start server**:
   ```bash

   ```

Set these **before** running `npm run db:setup` if your PostgreSQL uses different admin credentials:

```bash
# Windows PowerShell
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_admin_user"
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_admin_password"

# Windows CMD
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=your_admin_user
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=your_admin_password
```

**Defaults:**
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres`
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres`
- `DB_HOST=localhost`
- `DB_PORT=5432`

### Generated Variables (Auto-written to .env)

After running `npm run db:setup`, your `.env` file will contain:

```env
# Database Configuration (Auto-generated by setup-postgres.js)
POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres
POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres
DB_HOST=localhost
DB_PORT=5432
DB_NAME=emdad_3pl
DB_USER=emdad_3pl_app
DB_PASSWORD=<32-character-hex-password>
DATABASE_URL="postgresql://emdad_3pl_app:<password>@localhost:5432/emdad_3pl?schema=public"
```

## 🔌 How Backend Reads Database Configuration

**Connection Flow:**
```
.env or .env.local
  ↓
DATABASE_URL environment variable
  ↓
Prisma schema.prisma (datasource db { url = env("DATABASE_URL") })
  ↓
PrismaClient (generated)
  ↓
PrismaService (extends PrismaClient)
  ↓
Application Code (inventory.service.ts, etc.)
```

**Key Points:**
- NestJS `ConfigModule` loads `.env.local` (preferred) or `.env` (fallback)
- Prisma reads `DATABASE_URL` from environment
- All database operations go through `PrismaService`

## ✅ Setup Steps

1. **Ensure PostgreSQL is running** on your local machine

2. **Set admin credentials** (if different from defaults):
   ```powershell
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_user"
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_password"
   ```

3. **Run setup**:
   ```bash
   npm run db:setup
   ```

4. **Generate Prisma client**:
   ```bash
   npm run prisma:generate
   ```

5. **Seed database** (optional):
   ```bash
   npm run db:seed
   ```

6. **Start server**:
   ```bash
   npm run start:dev
   ```

## 🔍 Verification

After setup, verify everything works:

```bash
# Test connection
npm run db:check

# View data in Prisma Studio
npm run prisma:studio

# Test API endpoint
# Start server, then: GET http://localhost:3000/inventory/current-stock
```

## 🛠️ Troubleshooting

### "password authentication failed"
- Your PostgreSQL admin credentials are incorrect
- Set `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER` and `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD` before running setup

### "connection refused"
- PostgreSQL is not running
- Check if PostgreSQL service is started
- Verify it's listening on port 5432

### "database already exists"
- Normal if you've run setup before
- Script will skip creation and continue
- Use `npm run db:reset` to start fresh

## 📚 Additional Documentation

- **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup instructions and troubleshooting
- **`QUICK_START.md`** - General project quick start
- **`DATABASE_SETUP.md`** - Manual setup alternatives

## 🎉 You're Ready!

The database setup is fully automated. Just run `npm run db:setup` and you're done!

**That's it!** The script handles everything automatically.

## 📁 Files Created

### Setup Scripts
1. **`scripts/setup-postgres.js`** - Main automated setup script
   - Creates database user
   - Creates database
   - Grants privileges
   - Runs schema.sql
   - Updates .env file

2. **`scripts/reset-database.js`** - Database reset script
   - Drops and recreates database
   - Useful for development resets

3. **`scripts/check-postgres.js`** - Connection test script
   - Verifies PostgreSQL connectivity

### Configuration Files
4. **`.env.example`** - Environment variables template
   - Shows all required variables
   - Safe to commit to version control

### Documentation
5. **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup guide
6. **`DATABASE_SETUP_SUMMARY.md`** - Quick reference
7. **`POSTGRES_SETUP_COMPLETE.md`** - This file

### Updated Files
8. **`package.json`** - Added database scripts:
   - `db:setup` - Full setup
   - `db:reset` - Reset database
   - `db:check` - Test connection
   - `db:seed` - Seed fake data

## 🔧 Available NPM Scripts

| Command | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `npm run db:setup` | **Full automated setup** - Creates user, database, runs schema |
| `npm run db:reset` | Drop and recreate database (WARNING: deletes all data) |
| `npm run db:check` | Test PostgreSQL connection |
| `npm run db:seed` | Seed database with fake data |
| `npm run prisma:generate` | Generate Prisma client after setup |
| `npm run prisma:studio` | Open Prisma Studio to view data |

## 📝 Environment Variables

### Setup Variables (Optional - for custom admin credentials)

Set these **before** running `npm run db:setup` if your PostgreSQL uses different admin credentials:

```bash
# Windows PowerShell
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_admin_user"
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_admin_password"

# Windows CMD
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=your_admin_user
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=your_admin_password
```

**Defaults:**
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres`
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres`
- `DB_HOST=localhost`
- `DB_PORT=5432`

### Generated Variables (Auto-written to .env)

After running `npm run db:setup`, your `.env` file will contain:

```env
# Database Configuration (Auto-generated by setup-postgres.js)
POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres
POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres
DB_HOST=localhost
DB_PORT=5432
DB_NAME=emdad_3pl
DB_USER=emdad_3pl_app
DB_PASSWORD=<32-character-hex-password>
DATABASE_URL="postgresql://emdad_3pl_app:<password>@localhost:5432/emdad_3pl?schema=public"
```

## 🔌 How Backend Reads Database Configuration

**Connection Flow:**
```
.env or .env.local
  ↓
DATABASE_URL environment variable
  ↓
Prisma schema.prisma (datasource db { url = env("DATABASE_URL") })
  ↓
PrismaClient (generated)
  ↓
PrismaService (extends PrismaClient)
  ↓
Application Code (inventory.service.ts, etc.)
```

**Key Points:**
- NestJS `ConfigModule` loads `.env.local` (preferred) or `.env` (fallback)
- Prisma reads `DATABASE_URL` from environment
- All database operations go through `PrismaService`

## ✅ Setup Steps

1. **Ensure PostgreSQL is running** on your local machine

2. **Set admin credentials** (if different from defaults):
   ```powershell
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_user"
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_password"
   ```

3. **Run setup**:
   ```bash
   npm run db:setup
   ```

4. **Generate Prisma client**:
   ```bash
   npm run prisma:generate
   ```

5. **Seed database** (optional):
   ```bash
   npm run db:seed
   ```

6. **Start server**:
   ```bash
   npm run start:dev
   ```

## 🔍 Verification

After setup, verify everything works:

```bash
# Test connection
npm run db:check

# View data in Prisma Studio
npm run prisma:studio

# Test API endpoint
# Start server, then: GET http://localhost:3000/inventory/current-stock
```

## 🛠️ Troubleshooting

### "password authentication failed"
- Your PostgreSQL admin credentials are incorrect
- Set `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER` and `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD` before running setup

### "connection refused"
- PostgreSQL is not running
- Check if PostgreSQL service is started
- Verify it's listening on port 5432

### "database already exists"
- Normal if you've run setup before
- Script will skip creation and continue
- Use `npm run db:reset` to start fresh

## 📚 Additional Documentation

- **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup instructions and troubleshooting
- **`QUICK_START.md`** - General project quick start
- **`DATABASE_SETUP.md`** - Manual setup alternatives

## 🎉 You're Ready!

The database setup is fully automated. Just run `npm run db:setup` and you're done!

   ```

## 🔍 Verification

After setup, verify everything works:

```bash
# Test connection
npm run db:check

# View data in Prisma Studio
npm run prisma:studio

# Test API endpoint
# Start server, then: GET http://localhost:3000/inventory/current-stock
```

## 🛠️ Troubleshooting

### "password authentication failed"
- Your PostgreSQL admin credentials are incorrect
- Set `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER` and `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD` before running setup

### "connection refused"
- PostgreSQL is not running
- Check if PostgreSQL service is started
- Verify it's listening on port 5432

### "database already exists"
- Normal if you've run setup before
- Script will skip creation and continue
- Use `npm run db:reset` to start fresh

## 📚 Additional Documentation

- **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup instructions and troubleshooting
- **`QUICK_START.md`** - General project quick start
- **`DATABASE_SETUP.md`** - Manual setup alternatives

## 🎉 You're Ready!

The database setup is fully automated. Just run `npm run db:setup` and you're done!




## 🎯 Summary

Automated PostgreSQL database setup has been configured for the Emdad 3PL WMS backend. All scripts and configuration files are ready to use.

## 📋 Generated Database Credentials

When you run the setup script, it will automatically generate:

- **Database Name**: `emdad_3pl`
- **Database User**: `emdad_3pl_app`  
- **Database Password**: Randomly generated secure password (32 hex characters)
- **Host**: `localhost`
- **Port**: `5432`

## 🚀 Quick Start Command

```bash
cd server
npm run db:setup
```

**That's it!** The script handles everything automatically.

## 📁 Files Created

### Setup Scripts
1. **`scripts/setup-postgres.js`** - Main automated setup script
   - Creates database user
   - Creates database
   - Grants privileges
   - Runs schema.sql
   - Updates .env file

2. **`scripts/reset-database.js`** - Database reset script
   - Drops and recreates database
   - Useful for development resets

3. **`scripts/check-postgres.js`** - Connection test script
   - Verifies PostgreSQL connectivity

### Configuration Files
4. **`.env.example`** - Environment variables template
   - Shows all required variables
   - Safe to commit to version control

### Documentation
5. **`SETUP_POSTGRES.md`** - Detailed setup guide
6. **`DATABASE_SETUP_SUMMARY.md`** - Quick reference
7. **`POSTGRES_SETUP_COMPLETE.md`** - This file

### Updated Files
8. **`package.json`** - Added database scripts:
   - `db:setup` - Full setup
   - `db:reset` - Reset database
   - `db:check` - Test connection
   - `db:seed` - Seed fake data

## 🔧 Available NPM Scripts

| Command | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| `npm run db:setup` | **Full automated setup** - Creates user, database, runs schema |
| `npm run db:reset` | Drop and recreate database (WARNING: deletes all data) |
| `npm run db:check` | Test PostgreSQL connection |
| `npm run db:seed` | Seed database with fake data |
| `npm run prisma:generate` | Generate Prisma client after setup |
| `npm run prisma:studio` | Open Prisma Studio to view data |

## 📝 Environment Variables

### Setup Variables (Optional - for custom admin credentials)

Set these **before** running `npm run db:setup` if your PostgreSQL uses different admin credentials:

```bash
# Windows PowerShell
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_admin_user"
$env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_admin_password"

# Windows CMD
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=your_admin_user
set POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=your_admin_password
```

**Defaults:**
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres`
- `POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres`
- `DB_HOST=localhost`
- `DB_PORT=5432`

### Generated Variables (Auto-written to .env)

After running `npm run db:setup`, your `.env` file will contain:

```env
# Database Configuration (Auto-generated by setup-postgres.js)
POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER=postgres
POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD=postgres
DB_HOST=localhost
DB_PORT=5432
DB_NAME=emdad_3pl
DB_USER=emdad_3pl_app
DB_PASSWORD=<32-character-hex-password>
DATABASE_URL="postgresql://emdad_3pl_app:<password>@localhost:5432/emdad_3pl?schema=public"
```

## 🔌 How Backend Reads Database Configuration

**Connection Flow:**
```
.env or .env.local
  ↓
DATABASE_URL environment variable
  ↓
Prisma schema.prisma (datasource db { url = env("DATABASE_URL") })
  ↓
PrismaClient (generated)
  ↓
PrismaService (extends PrismaClient)
  ↓
Application Code (inventory.service.ts, etc.)
```

**Key Points:**
- NestJS `ConfigModule` loads `.env.local` (preferred) or `.env` (fallback)
- Prisma reads `DATABASE_URL` from environment
- All database operations go through `PrismaService`

## ✅ Setup Steps

1. **Ensure PostgreSQL is running** on your local machine

2. **Set admin credentials** (if different from defaults):
   ```powershell
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_USER="your_user"
   $env:POSTGRES_ADMIN_PASSWORD="your_password"
   ```

3. **Run setup**:
   ```bash
   npm run db:setup
   ```

4. **Generate Prisma client**:
   ```bash
   npm run prisma:generate
   ```

5. **Seed database** (optional):
   ```bash
   npm run db:seed
   ```

6. **Start server**:
   ```bash
   npm run start:dev
   ```

## 🔍 Verification

After setup, verify everything works:

```bash
# Test connection
npm run db:check

# View data in Prisma Studio

# Test API endpoint
# Start server, then: GET http://localhost:3000/inventory/current-stock
```

### "connection refused"

- Check if PostgreSQL service is started
- Verify it's listening on port 5432

### "database already exists"
- Normal if you've run setup before
- Script will skip creation and continue
- Use `npm run db:reset` to start fresh
